## Text Elements
Linked List ^netDMXGB

- Linked List can be defined as collection of objects called nodes that are randomly stored in the memory.

- A node contains two fields i.e. data stored at that particular address and the pointer which contains the address of the next node in the memory.

- The last node of the list contains pointer to the null. ^0B5LfyGf

- Nodes that have no links pointing to them except for the head node, are considered “orphaned.”  ^Pr5CFOsU

A NULL value in the link part of a node’s info denotes that the path or data structure contains no further nodes. ^9Li86pny

- After all the nodes have been printed the head becomes null and the program flow breaks;
- But as head = null, now we can print the list again! 
- Hence this method can not be used for displaying nodes of linked list but only for when we want to change change structure of the whole list! ^qjRmOc6y

Insertion in Linked List  ^FtOuRvnL

- If a element is supposed to be entered in before the header than that can be easily done by making space for the new node by moving the initial head to the next node and assigning value of the new node to be as a head node now. ^0EtLCO87

- If I want to add the new node with value assigned to be 3 then I will have to break the link b/w 2 and 4 and make the node.next of 2 to be 3 and then node.next of 3 to be 4. And that's how the chain of linked list works.    ^hqEbwjS1

- For delete operation to work anywhere traverse back to the node which is to be deleted. Then the previous node of the selected node make it to point to the next node of selected node for deletion. Also now as the link to the selected node is broken it can be said it has been deleted. ^2zCbDDta

- s moves 1 node ...
- f moves 2 node ...
...at a time in each iterations ^Cnu5Y4rv

- Both space and time complexity if O(n). ^8LJ9kKOG

- To calculate length of cycle keep the fast 
pointer in the same place and complete 
a cycle with slow pointer. Once fast 
pointer and slow pointer meet again 
the number of movement is length of cycle. ^mfjG3aAU

Steps to Reverse a Linked List Recursively

- Base Case: 
If the head is null or if the head's next node is null, return the head. This means we have 
reached the end of the list or the list is empty.

- Recursive Case: 
Call the reverse function on the next node (head.next). After the recursive call returns, 
set the next node's next pointer to the current node (head). Set the current node's next 
pointer to null to avoid cycles.

- Return the new head: 
The new head of the reversed list will be the return value of the recursive call. ^tGvILlJt

5 ^L5Ivtjyo

head ^mXGGh7FV

tail ^iBJbVjN7

- We take 3 pointers :
    previous = null
    present = head
    next = head.next  ^VO0jKeGK

pr.next = pv
pv = pr
pr = next
next = next.next ^yNZrngXv

- next.next can throw null pointer exception ^m3id12Pd

- Once the iteration is complete and all pointers have been reversed, the prev pointer, which now points to the new head of the reversed list, is set as the new head of the list. 
- This results in the linked list being completely reversed, with its head now at the former tail. ^kNMwhSGc
